WELL EVALUATION
QEP Energy Company
Moberg 20-17-19-18LL
Figure 1: Unit Rig #121 on the Moberg 20-17-19-18LL, Jan. 2015.
INTRODUCTION
QEP Energy Company's Moberg 20-17-19-18LL [SW SW Sec. 20, T149N, R95W] is located
approximately 25 miles southeast of Watford City, North Dakota. The Moberg 20-17-19-18LL
is proposed as a 1,280-acre stand up spacing unit that straddles 4 sections. The 10,000' lateral is
targeting the Three Forks Formation within the Grail & Bear Den Fields of the Williston Basin.
This lateral will be drilled from south to north within sections 20, 17, 19 & 18. Sections 20, 17 &
19 are within the Grail Field and section 18 in the Bear Den Field. The Moberg 20-17-19-18LL
will be the first of two Three Forks wells on the pad drilled to completion.
OFFSET WELLS
Primary offset wells used in correlation with the Moberg 20-17-19-18LL, were QEP Energy
Company's Moberg 3-20-21TH, Moberg 2-20-21TH, both located within 1,250' to the
northwest. The QEP Energy Company's Moberg 4-20/21H located north of the Moberg 20-21-
29-28LL provided the third offset. These wells all included very similar isopach and interval
thicknesses. This information helped to determine relative projections and illustrations when
drilling the vertical, and building an accurate curve. All offsets were expected to provide reliable
data as they too were drilled into the Three Forks Formation.
OPERATIONS
The Moberg 20-17-19-18LL was spud on January 10, 2015 by Unit Drilling Rig #121.
Previously a 13 ½" hole was drilled with fresh water to 2,132' MD, and isolated with 9 5/8"
casing cemented to surface. Once the surface hole was complete, the drilling fluid was then
switched to diesel invert for the vertical and curve. The vertical hole was drilled to our kickoff
point for the curve build at 10,540' MD. Halliburton provided all tools, directional, and MWD
personnel. The gamma ray probe and curve assembly were picked up at kick off on January 16,
2015, and the curve was completed at 11,360' MD on January 17, 2015. Upon completing the
curve 7' casing was set and cemented to 11,343' MD. A total of 5 BHA's were used to drill
surface hole to intermediate casing point.
Prior to drilling the lateral diesel based drilling fluid was changed over to salt water based
drilling fluid. The lateral section of the Moberg 20-17-19-18LL began on the 21st of January,
2015 and would be the first lateral completed on the pad. The Moberg 20-17-19-18LL was
drilled from intermediate casing point to total depth using 2 BHA's at 20,923' MD and 11,016'
TVD in 7 drilling days, on the 26th of January, 2015 at 22:18 CT. The bottom hole is located at
10,023.05' N & 522.28' W of surface location or approximately 250.62' FNL & 27.72' FWL, NW
NW Sec. 17, T149N, R95W.
GEOLOGY
Methods
All geologic personnel and analysis for Moberg 20-17-19-18LL was provided by Sunburst
Consulting, Inc. Our gas, rate of penetration, and all other drilling parameters were delivered via
Pason's electronic data recorder system. Total gas was measured in units, using a 10,000 unit
scale. Beginning at 6,000' MD, rig crews caught lagged samples at the direction of the well site
geologists. Samples were collected at 30' intervals throughout the vertical and curve. Two sets of
dry cuttings were collected for QEP Energy Company, one of which was sent to the North
Dakota Geological Survey. Rock cuttings were analyzed in wet and dry conditions under a
20x60 power binocular microscope.
Prospective Intervals
The thickness of the Mission Canyon Formation was 597' TVD. The upper section varied from
lime wackestone to mudstone and contained dark brown algal laminations with fair amounts of
anhydrite throughout the formation. The middle to lower sections primarily consisted of
argillaceous limestone described as firm mudstone, light gray to tan in color with an earthy
texture. The Mission Canyon once again showed traces of light brown oil staining in the lower
half of the formation. Background gas throughout the formation remained between 100 to 300
units. Similar to the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL, gas throughout this formation was lower in
relation to other wells in the area.
The Lodgepole Formation was 866' TVD, and consisted of
argillaceous lime mudstone and wackestone. These samples are
described as light to medium gray, earthy in texture, and grading
from firm to moderately hard. It also included traces of algal
laminations and disseminated pyrite. Background gas in the
Lodgepole throughout the upper and middle sections once again
remained low between 100 to 300 units. The gas jumped quickly
at 10,619' MD to 750 units. This was the beginning of an ever
increasing trend of gas throughout the remainder of the vertical
and curve portions of the well. Gas held steadily near 500 units
until a measured depth of 10,888' where during a connection, gas
shot up to 5,581 units. It was at this depth the gas quickly
elevated and never dropped below 659 units, peaking at a
Figure 2: Limestone from the
respectable 4,348 units.
Lodgepole Formation.
The Scallion Member, located at the base of the Lodgepole
formation, was 12' TVD in thickness. This member is composed
of a moderately hard and platy limestone with waxy texture,
traces of nodular pyrite, and light brown oil staining. One
legitimate show of gas occurred at 11,020' MD which reached
2,654 units.
The Upper Bakken Shale was 20' TVD in thickness and made up
of soft to friable sub-blocky and petroliferous black shale. This
shale has a consistent distribution of disseminated pyrite. The
Upper Bakken Shale's high gamma signature and abundant oil
shows are distinguishing characteristics. Also common for this
area is a high concentration of gas which averaged over 4,000
Figure 3: Upper Bakken Shale
units, and peaked at 5,909 units.
The Middle Bakken was 39' in thickness. The upper most
portion of the Middle Bakken consists most notably of
carbonaceous and calcareous siltstone. This upper facies was
described as being medium gray to dark gray in color, soft,
showing common spotty brown oil stain, and having calcareous
cement. Underlying the siltstone facies lies a limestone interval
with abundant fossil fragments and oil staining. This interval,
also known as "packstone", has a hard waxy texture and typically
difficult to drill in. The lower portion of the Middle Bakken is
silty sandstone which emits a "ratty" gamma signature consisting
of API peaks tightly alternating from 70 to 90 units. The lower
Figure 4: Silty sandstone from
the Middle Bakken.
facies is defined as a light to medium gray-brown silty
sandstone. It ranges from fine to very fine grained, and consists
of calcareous cement, intergranular porosity and traces of light
brown oil staining. Background gases here remained well
elevated, averaging over 4,400 units.
The Lower Bakken Shale was drilled for 32' TVD, and 95' of
MD. This shale was dark brown to black, sub-blocky, with an
earthy texture. It is also carbonaceous and highly petroliferous.
Background gases throughout the Lower Bakken Shale
averaged over 4,200 units, and peaked on a connection at
11,199' MD at 4,850 units.
Figure 5: Black shale from the
Lower Bakken.
Three Forks target geology & gas show
The target zone within this Three Forks lateral was set at 20'
thick. The top of the target window starts at the "hot" gamma
ray marker, or approximately 10' below the Lower Bakken
Shale. This high gamma ray signature consists of light blue to
light green shale with traces of interbedded dolomite, and
creates a signature marker for positioning within the target. The
next 20' TVD of isopach consists of laminated shale and
dolomite which QEP refers to as the "laminated section". This
interval is described as light blue to light green calcareous shale
with interbedded tan to brown dolomite. Underlying the
"laminated section" is the "massive dolomite" which consists of
soft argillaceous tan dolomite with abundant unconsolidated and
well disseminated sandstone.
Figure 6: Dolomitic siltstone
within the Three Forks.
Samples collected during the extent of the lateral consisted primarily of light blue shale and tan
dolomite. The dolomite within the samples varied, which graded from non-calcareous
mineralized dolomite to soft and slightly calcareous argillaceous dolomite. The more dolomitized
rock appeared darker in color and typically ranged from medium to dark brown. Throughout the
target zone, disseminated pyrite and oil staining was evident in the samples. Color variations of
the rocks helped determine target positioning throughout the lateral.
Background gas in the first part of the lateral remained between 1,000 to 1,500 units. The first
significant gas show appeared at 14,100' to 16,200', where the wellbore dropped near the bottom
of target zone. Gas within this show ranged from 2,000 to 6,000 units. Upon contact with the
bottom portion of the target, massive gas increases were seen throughout the middle portion of
the lateral. The latter part of the lateral was drilled in the middle to upper portion of the target
zone where gas shows were noticeably less intense ranging from 700 to 1,100 units.
GEO-STEERING
QEP's pre-drill plan for the Moberg 20-17-19-18LL suggested a regional 0.02° upward dip for a
majority of the lateral. The hot gamma ray marker consistent with the top of the target was not
encountered during the lateral however the "massive dolomite" was briefly encountered three
times providing great stratigraphic positioning for geo-steering. The "massive dolomite" was
very close to QEP's structural pre-drill estimations. Due to the close relativity of structure and
dip pre-drill estimations, only very slight changes were made throughout the lateral to adjust the
planned profile. Attempts were made to correlate repeating gamma signatures as well as sample
cutting analysis to determine wellbore positioning within the target zone. Overall regional dip for
the Moberg 20-17-19-18LL was 0.20° upward with 34' TVD of structural ascension. The lateral
was successfully geosteered 98% within the target zone by QEP's geology team, Sunburst
Consulting and Halliburton's directional drillers

SUMMARY
The Moberg 20-17-19-18LL vertical and curve was drilled from spud to Intermediate Casing
Point in 9 drilling days. The curve was landed as planned on January 17, 2015.
Samples within the lower Lodgepole Formation showed spotty oil staining, upon reaching the
Upper Bakken and Lower Bakken Shale members abundant oil was observed at the shakers and
in cuttings with slight oil pooling observed in the shakers. Sample cuttings throughout the target
zone also showed consistent spotty brown oil stain. Background and connection gas increased
significantly from 14,100' to 16,200' MD reaching up to 6,000 units.
The Moberg 20-17-19-18LL lateral was drilled from Intermediate Casing Point to Total Depth in
7 drilling days for a total of 18 drilling days from spud to finish. The lateral reached TD at
20.923' MD on the 26th of January, 2015. Overall the Moberg 20-17-19-18LL was drilled
successfully 98% within the designated target zone, and shows good potential for production.
Respectfully,
Eric Peters
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
Moberg 20-17-19-18LL
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A detailed list of sampling
intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray marker tops have been inserted in the sample
descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Sample descriptions
begin in the Swift Formation. Diesel invert drilling fluid was used for the vertical and curve while Water based drilling fluid
was used for the lateral portions of the well.
6,000-6,030
SILTSTONE: dark gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, sandy grained in part, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,030-6,060
SHALE: light green gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,060-6,090
SHALE: light green gray, trace medium gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace
disseminated pyrite, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,090-6,120
SHALE: light green gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain
6,120-6,150
SHALE: light gray, firm, rare friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no
visible porosity or oil stain
6,150-6,180
SHALE: light gray, firm, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain
6,180-6,210
SHALE: light green gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain
6,210-6,240
SHALE: light gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain
6,240-6,270
SHALE: light gray, friable, occasional firm, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite,
no visible porosity or oil stain
6,270-6,300
SHALE: light gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain; occasional SILTSTONE: red brown, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, calcareous cement,
moderately cemented, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,300-6,330
SHALE: light gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain; abundant SILTSTONE: red brown, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, calcareous cement,
moderately cemented, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,330-6,360
SHALE: light gray, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible
porosity or oil stain; common SILTSTONE: red brown, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, calcareous cement,
moderately cemented, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,360-6,390
SILTSTONE: dark brown, friable, sub-blocky-sub-platy, earthy texture, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, no visible porosity or oil stain
6,390-6,420

microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, dense, no visible porosity or oil stain

Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 300' west. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the
well head is: 10073' north.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.

Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov

RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

NOTES ON 9-5/8" SURFACE CASING DESIGN:
The key point in designing surface casing is to extend the shoe of the surface casing beyond the top of
the Pierre Shale. This ensures that all potable or usable water zones are covered. At this point in the well
design, the drilling fluid is changed to oil base mud to contend with salt sections that occur at
approximately 7,000' TVD and 9,375' TVD. The 36 ppf J55 casing accomplishes these criteria easily.
A higher burst rating is not necessary based on industry standards throughout the Williston Basin.
In the event the surface casing burst rating was increased, the normally pressured and sub normally
pressured zones all the way thru the Madison Group at approximately 8,750' TVD has the potential to
break down. Therefore the increased pressure rating of surface casing is not warranted. It is not feasible
to set the surface casing point at a greater depth because the shut in surface pressures would not
appreciably increase. The Dakota formation (5,350' TVD) is frequently weak. Typically, we drill the
intermediate section with 10.5 ppg OBM to the 7" casing point. In the event we lost circulation in the
exposed intermediate interval, the wellbore will not be entirely evacuated and the surface casing can be
shut in without compromising the pressure rating of the 36 ppf J-55.
Calculations for the Surface Casing Design:
3,520 psi/ (6,013 psi (Reservoir Pressure) ­ (11,013 ft x 0.22 psi/ft)) = safety factor of 1.0

No abnormal temperatures or pressures are anticipated. No H2S has been encountered in or known to
exist from previous wells drilled to similar depths in the general area. Maximum anticipated bottom
hole pressure equals approximately 6,013 psi. Maximum anticipated bottom hole temperature is 290° F.
10.
Additional Information For Oil Base Mud
A. Oil-base mud will be mixed in the closed circulating system and transferred to 500-bbl tanks on
location for storage prior to and after drilling operations. Drip pans will be installed below the
rotary beams on the substructure and can be viewed on site from the cellar area. As the intermediate
and production section of the hole is drilled, the cuttings transported to the surface with the drilling
fluid will be mechanically separated from the drilling fluid as waste by shale-shakers and then
cleaned/dried via a mud cleaner and/or centrifuge. These separated cuttings will be transferred to a
container, dried and stabilized, and then transported to an approved disposal site or, if a cuttings pit
is approved, the solidified and dried cuttings will be stored in the pit.
B. Plastic material will underlay the rig, oil base mud/diesel storage tanks and mud pits. All tanks on
location will be placed inside of berms. Any oily waste fluids and sediments generated at the work
site during drilling operations or when cleaning the fluid containment system after drilling will also
be stabilized and then transported to an approved disposal site or, if a cuttings pit is approved, it will
be solidified and stored in the cuttings pit.
C. All rig ditches will be lined and directed to a lined sump for fluid recovery. A drip pan will be
installed on the BOP stack, a mud bucket will be utilized as needed on connections and a vacuum
system will be used on the rig floor for fluid recovery in those areas.
Page 6 of 8
ONSHORE OIL & GAS ORDER NO. 1
QEP North Dakota Operations
Moberg 20-17-19-18LL
D. If a cuttings pit is deemed necessary and acceptable due to unforeseen circumstances and/or
complications with the disposal method described in 10.A above, drill solids and excess cement will
be placed in the cuttings pit and the oilfield waste management consultant Soli-Bond (or a similar
company) will mobilize equipment and personnel to the site to perform the cement based
solidification/stabilization process in-situ for encapsulation with cement kiln dust or flyash prior to
placement in the cuttings pit. Once the drilling operation is complete, the lined cuttings pit will be
reclaimed to grade elevation.

Gas Capture Plan (Moberg 13-20Y2 Pad ­ 2 wells)
1. Affidavit: attached as a part of this gas capture plan.
2. Detailed gas gathering pipeline system location map
Oneok Rockies Midstream ("OKRM")
Oneok existing trunkline
Name and Location of gas processing plant: Garden Creek Plant, Section 35-T151N-R98W.
Name of gas gatherer and location of lines for each gas gatherer in the vicinity: OKRM 16" poly
highlighted in red; contracted with OKRM until 2019, no other viable gatherers in the vicinity.
Proposed Route and Tie-in point for wel connection: See above gathering system map
3. Detailed information for Blue Buttes/Grail/Sandstone compression capacity (circled in blue):
Maximum current daily capacity: Total: 95 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 35; Grail: 0) Note: Grail
station expected to start-up in mid-September 2014.
Current throughput: Total: 82 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 22; Grail: 0) Note: Grail station
expected to start-up in mid-September 2014.
Anticipated daily capacity at date of first gas sales: Total: 130 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 35;
Grail: 35).
Anticipated throughput at date of first gas sales: Total: 130 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 35;
Grail: 35).
Gas gatherer issues or expansion plans for the area: Beginning September, 2014, OKRM has adequate
pipeline, processing plant and compression capacity for QEP's current and forecasted gas through mid-
2015. These midstream facilities were designed to handle approximately 70 MMcfd of QEP's gas.
Should future iterations of QEP's volume forecast exceed 70 MMcfd, QEP will require another OKRM
expansion for compression and pipelines and has alerted OKRM of this possibility.
4. Detailed flowback strategy:
Anticipated date of first production: 2nd Quarter, 2015

5. QEP flaring amounts:
Statewide percentage of gas flared for existing wells in the Bakken petroleum system: 53% for the most
recent month of July 2014 (28.0 MMcfd flared /52.5 MMcfd produced).
Field wide percentage of gas flared for this well: 64% in the Grail field for the most recent month of July
2014 (26.6 MMcfd flared/41.5 MMcfd produced).
6. QEP Alternatives to flaring:
Specific alternative systems available for consideration: When OKRM is at capacity or not connected,
QEP has considered and implemented JT conditioning skids for its flaring wel s. QEP has done this on 2
pads in Sections 33 & 35 of T149N-R95W (vendor Montana-Dakota). QEP also is looking at site usage for
a number of applications to include powering wellhead equipment, drilling rigs, gas lift, etc. Further,
QEP is installing gas-powered generators on our pads in the Mandaree field (FBIR) instead of using diesel
fuel (second half of 2014).
Details of flaring reductions if such alternative plans are implemented: No significant flaring reductions
have been achieved from our implemented or planned alternative systems thus far. However, the
Montana-Dakota JT skids do reduce our VOCs by 85% where they are installed.
